  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b8b75a44-146a-46c7-b667-d61719efc1da'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_315767366" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315767366" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315767366?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315767366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17700937420562640117">This is called volume 13, and an encyclopedia for the series. It isn't really either. It's more like a set of DVD special features. Worth reading? Actually... yes, at least in part. The character profiles that start the book have very little new information to add, but L.'s does include his real name. The creator interviews that take up much of the space are actually really informative. There's a detailed timeline, a complete set of all the Death Note rules, and answers to most of the questions </span>
  <span id="freeText17700937420562640117" style="display:none">This is called volume 13, and an encyclopedia for the series. It isn't really either. It's more like a set of DVD special features. Worth reading? Actually... yes, at least in part. The character profiles that start the book have very little new information to add, but L.'s does include his real name. The creator interviews that take up much of the space are actually really informative. There's a detailed timeline, a complete set of all the Death Note rules, and answers to most of the questions a reader could have at this point that does have an answer. At the end are a series of (only vaguely amusing) four panel comics, and the original pilot chapter of Death Note. It's hugely different in tone, and I have to say that I'm very glad of the changes that were made. I don't know if I'd have read past the first volume if it had stayed like the pilot. My favorite part, though, was Ryuk's sarcastic commentary. For a fan, this is a must-read, but I'd say anybody who read the entire series should at least skim over the creator interviews.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17700937420562640117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Marjolein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marjolein" href="/user/show/5289598-marjolein">Marjolein</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289598-marjolein?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289598-marjolein?shelf=manga-comics-graphic-novels">manga-comics-graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer368187427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12550556185466974141"><i> Read all my reviews on <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com'>http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com</a> </i><br/><br/>I actually apologize because it took me almost four years to finish the book. Problem is, I don't usually get into reading a book that goes into such detail about a book I've just read, so I had some troubles to focus at the time and let it slide for a long time. <br/><br/>Now I was back at it, and it had been a while, so it all made more sense, since I was looking for some real Death Note after seeing the thing Netflix recently brought out. This</span>
  <span id="freeText12550556185466974141" style="display:none"><i> Read all my reviews on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com">http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com</a> </i><br /><br />I actually apologize because it took me almost four years to finish the book. Problem is, I don't usually get into reading a book that goes into such detail about a book I've just read, so I had some troubles to focus at the time and let it slide for a long time. <br /><br />Now I was back at it, and it had been a while, so it all made more sense, since I was looking for some real Death Note after seeing the thing Netflix recently brought out. This 13th collection contains a lot of information, though not necessarily new information. Character files, an explanation for all the chapter titles in the series, all the rules from the Death Note. And L's real name. <br /><br />Also, there are interviews with the creators and a pilot chapter, which was actually a lot of fun to read, even though if it had stayed on that path, it had been a completely different kind of series. However, I would only recommend this to the real fans of the series that can't get enough of it. For the rest of us, I think it might be a bit too detailed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12550556185466974141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2250660340" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2250660340" />
    <a title="Hamnah Siddiqui" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71363178-hamnah-siddiqui"><img alt="Hamnah Siddiqui" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2250660340?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamnah Siddiqui" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamnah Siddiqui" href="/user/show/71363178-hamnah-siddiqui">Hamnah Siddiqui</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2250660340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10796191154511768106">Death Note is a series by Tsugumi Ohba and Takeshi Obata about an epic battle of wits between the highschool student Light Yagami and detective extraordinaire L. Light found a notebook called the Death Note and uses it to kill criminals by writing their names in it. This causes him to be known by the public as Kira, or killer. L is determined to stop him and tries to do this by getting closer to Light and by having him work on the case with him. L almost exposed Light, but Light has supernatural</span>
  <span id="freeText10796191154511768106" style="display:none">Death Note is a series by Tsugumi Ohba and Takeshi Obata about an epic battle of wits between the highschool student Light Yagami and detective extraordinaire L. Light found a notebook called the Death Note and uses it to kill criminals by writing their names in it. This causes him to be known by the public as Kira, or killer. L is determined to stop him and tries to do this by getting closer to Light and by having him work on the case with him. L almost exposed Light, but Light has supernatural beings on his side which ultimately led to L's downfall. After L, his successors Near and Mello take the wheel of the Kira investigation and catch Light, but not before many others die. The 13th volume is not part of the story line, but does tie up any loose ends of the series. It also gives information about the characters that has not been revealed in the previous books and Q and A's with the authors. I rated this book a 5 out of 5 stars because it doesn't fail to live up to the high standards from the previous books and provides a sense of closure to the series. It also isn't boring and monotonous like most other guides or encyclopedias. I would recommend this book to those who have finished the series and have questions about the series, whether if it is about the characters' actions or thoughts, or if it is about the authors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10796191154511768106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1889852-lindsay?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42582702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3934901395566034326">I really enjoyed this Death Note volume 13. Of course, you don't read this manga to get more Death Note story, but rather to get a deeper understanding of the manga. This manga is more like the behind the scenes on a DVD. The creators answer many questions about all sorts of different things, explain different events in the manga, and make it more clear. I enjoyed reading the interviews with the creators, and it made my day to discover that their favorite character L! Both of them! <3 I also fou</span>
  <span id="freeText3934901395566034326" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this Death Note volume 13. Of course, you don't read this manga to get more Death Note story, but rather to get a deeper understanding of the manga. This manga is more like the behind the scenes on a DVD. The creators answer many questions about all sorts of different things, explain different events in the manga, and make it more clear. I enjoyed reading the interviews with the creators, and it made my day to discover that their favorite character L! Both of them! &lt;3 I also found it interesting to learn more of Ohba and Obata's personalities.<br /><br />This book is complete with in-depth character analysis es, a deeper explanation of the shinigami, an individual interview with both Ohba and Obata, explanations behind each chapter title, Death Note "truths" (such as the truth behind L's percentages), the important dates and the events that take place between them, design concepts behind characters, Ryuk's "Human Observation Notebook" with humorous details and a character personality quiz for the reader, and of course the four panel comics and Pilot. To me, however the interviews with Ohba and Obata were the most interesting, because I was able to learn things such as why Ohba did things the way he did to advance the plot in the way he wanted it to go. Perhaps it's because I'm obsessed with writing, but I loved reading about that. <br /><br />I recommend this to anyone who is an intellectual Death Note fan. If you read Death Note just for the action and the story, and couldn't care less about the reasons behind the story going the way it did, then you really don't have to read this. You'll probably get bored by everything except Pilot and the four panel comics, and perhaps Ryuk's human observation notebook. Unless you're willing to sit down and think, you really won't enjoy this book much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3934901395566034326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90075871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90075871" />
    <a title="Jeffrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1398540-jeffrey"><img alt="Jeffrey" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90075871?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey" href="/user/show/1398540-jeffrey">Jeffrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Death Note fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1398540-jeffrey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1398540-jeffrey?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1398540-jeffrey?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1398540-jeffrey?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1398540-jeffrey?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90075871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16898505687685822977">Vol 13 claims to be "the ultimate Death Note encyclopedia" but it comes off more as a DVD Special Features section. It includes some filler profiles on the characters and timelines out the events of the story and the movements of the death notes themselves. Most of it is written in tiny print, yet in an oversized volume and an upcharged cover price. There are also some four panel comics from various magazines in the original printing which are cute but largely forgettable.<br/><br/>The real value comes fr</span>
  <span id="freeText16898505687685822977" style="display:none">Vol 13 claims to be "the ultimate Death Note encyclopedia" but it comes off more as a DVD Special Features section. It includes some filler profiles on the characters and timelines out the events of the story and the movements of the death notes themselves. Most of it is written in tiny print, yet in an oversized volume and an upcharged cover price. There are also some four panel comics from various magazines in the original printing which are cute but largely forgettable.<br /><br />The real value comes from interviews with the creators: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1978.Tsugumi_Ohba" title="Tsugumi Ohba" rel="nofollow noopener">Tsugumi Ohba</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1978.Tsugumi_Ohba" title="Tsugumi Ohba" rel="nofollow noopener">Takeshi Obata</a>. While most of the questions fit standard pop questionnaire fare, there are some insights, especially from Obata, into the creative process and working relationship. <br /><br />It also includes the Death Note pilot which isn't bad, but the author clearly further developed his ideas before launching the real comic. <br /><br />There's about a third to a half a volume of real content in here and they packed it with other forgettable extras. I wouldn't spend full price for this volume but it's worth library-ing, or buying at discount, if you can find it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16898505687685822977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2374278715" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2374278715" />
    <a title="Ben Truong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77170844-ben-truong"><img alt="Ben Truong" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2374278715?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ben Truong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ben Truong" href="/user/show/77170844-ben-truong">Ben Truong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77170844-ben-truong?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2374278715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7462814335452763269"><i>Death Note: How to Read</i> is less like an encyclopedia as advertised (perhaps styled as one), but more like a reference guide to the Death Note manga series. It includes character bios, story line summaries, interviews, production notes, commentaries, the pilot chapter of the manga, and includes <i>Ryuk's Human Observation Journal</i>. There are seven distinct sections to the book with many sub-sections for one to preview.<br/><br/>The first section of the tankobon is dedicated to the character profiles of every c</span>
  <span id="freeText7462814335452763269" style="display:none"><i>Death Note: How to Read</i> is less like an encyclopedia as advertised (perhaps styled as one), but more like a reference guide to the Death Note manga series. It includes character bios, story line summaries, interviews, production notes, commentaries, the pilot chapter of the manga, and includes <i>Ryuk's Human Observation Journal</i>. There are seven distinct sections to the book with many sub-sections for one to preview.<br /><br />The first section of the tankobon is dedicated to the character profiles of every character in the series – including the Shinigami. It is here that we find out L's real name, which was staring at our faces the whole time! While the character profile in this section doesn't change the story at all – it does enhance it somewhat. It is, I think, more relevant or interesting for those who like to make fanwork, in particular fanfiction. However, if you are to use the information from this section, please note that the translator has miscalculated their heights slight when converting from the metric system.<br /><br />The second to sixth sections of the tankobon is dedicated to the creators of the series. Here we find a timeline of the series (second section), which is rather helpful to fan creators to reference to when trying to remember how the sequence of events took place. There are also in-depth interviews with the creators, Tsugumi Ohba (third and sixth sections) and Takeshi Obata (fourth and sixth sections), where they reviewed how the story and illustrations were constructed respectively. The fifth section deals with the Death Note itself – how it's used, the rules, and all the tricks when using the <i>Death Note</i> – again it is a helpful reference – especially those interested in doing fanwork.<br /><br />The final section is perhaps the most entertaining of the tankobon, it includes observational notes from Ryuk on Light Yagami, L, Misa Amane, Mello, and Near. It also contains a <i>"What Death Note Character Are You?"</i> type quiz. It has several four-panel comics of the series, but the most intriguing part of this section and perhaps the entire tankobon is the Pilot Chapter of the series.<br /><br />Like a television pilot, manga series goes through the same thing, this pilot chapter is a one-shot that was published in <i>Weekly Shonen Jump</i> (No. 36, 2003) and did well enough that the story was picked up for serialization, leading to the first chapter of the manga series being published four months later in <i>Weekly Shonen Jump</i> (No. 01, 2004).<br /><br />It stars a thirteen-year-old Taro Kagami who finds a Death Note one day, but not knowing how to read English, he recognizes the second word Note and presumes it's a regular notebook and uses it as such, because he just lost his not too long ago. Everything went well until he wrote someone's name in the book and he dies. He eventually meets Ryuk and given the Death Eraser, which when used in the Death Note could erase what happened to them, provided they haven't been cremated, which Taro used and was glad to hear that the names he's written in the book were revived.<br /><br />Days later, Ryuk reveals that he lost his second Death Note and Taro finds another boy named Miura using the book for punishing criminals – Taro manages to convince the boy to go to the police and demonstrate the Death Note powers on himself in front of the police – he dies and resurrected again and the police took the second Death Note into custody and destroyed it by burning it, while Taro kept his in secret. Seven years later, Death Note has become a cultural phenomenon, where an older Taro Kagami and his Ryuk reads rumours of a Death Note being real in a magazine.<br /><br />While the pilot is interesting to read, I'm really glad that they got rid of the Death Eraser in the original series – it makes death finite, which it should be, and makes each name written in the Death Note holds more gravity. I'm also glad that they aged the main character, while giving a thirteen year old a Death Note would be interesting – it would be limited to what he could do with it.<br /><br />As an aside, the size of this tankobon is significantly bigger than the normal tankobon. If you're the type who likes all their manga tankobon looking with the same height (like me), then you should reconsider getting this tankobon as it is not necessary to read this book to enjoy the series.<br /><br />All in all, <i>Death Note: How to Read</i> is a wonderful reference book and the pilot chapter was also an interesting read – just to see where the idea of Death Note originated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7462814335452763269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3379008355" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello"><img alt="Michael Sorbello" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521124600p2/4307906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3379008355?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer9555834898934643383">This is a review of the entire series.<br/><br/>Synopsis: Light Yagami is an ace student with great prospects and he's bored out of his mind. But all that changes when he finds the Death Note, a notebook dropped by a rogue Shinigami, a death god. Any human whose name is written in the notebook dies, and now Light has vowed to use the power of the Death Note to rid the world of evil.   <span id="freeText9555834898934643383" style="display:none">This is a review of the entire series.<br /><br />Synopsis: Light Yagami is an ace student with great prospects and he's bored out of his mind. But all that changes when he finds the Death Note, a notebook dropped by a rogue Shinigami, a death god. Any human whose name is written in the notebook dies, and now Light has vowed to use the power of the Death Note to rid the world of evil. But when criminals begin dropping dead, the authorities send the legendary detective L to track down the killer. With L hot on his heels, will Light lose sight of his noble goal... or his life?<br /><br />Review: This series is intelligent, dark, full of suspense and makes clever use of metaphorical religious themes and imagery. It’s a look into what happens when great power falls into the hands of a young man named Light. Light is a collected, highly skilled and incredibly smart young man with the powerful urge to make the world a better place. The Death Note gives Light the ability to kill anyone at any time by writing their name down in the notebook and he aims to erase all criminals from the world, as well as innocent people that may try to get in the way of his morally flawed goal.<br /><br />Light becomes corrupted by the power to choose when people die and we are subjected to watching an idealistic young hero slowly reveal himself to be a narcissistic sociopath with a god complex. Light is cunning and charismatic, yet he’s also petty and spiteful. You'll find yourself rooting for him as often as you'll find yourself hating him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9555834898934643383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I believe I have read enough of it to give it a rating, and what I did read just didn't seem to add to my knowledge of </span>
  <span id="freeText10494059164467289356" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br />So I've been "reading" this book for a very long time, but have ultimately DNF'd it due to taking so long to finish it. I have simply lost interest. When I had initially finished the Death Note manga, I was keen to absorb as much of the series' content as I could. Now, after spending significant time apart from the series I simply do not care what this book has to say. I believe I have read enough of it to give it a rating, and what I did read just didn't seem to add to my knowledge of Death Note. It doesn't really say anything we didn't already know or learn from reading the manga itself, and any "extra" bits I just wasn't interested in.<br />It is an okay volume, but a die-hard Death Note fan would likely love it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1774045675034832344">Alright this is a really really good book to read once you've finished the Death Note series. It doesn't contain any more canon story, but it's full of character profiles and interviews with Tsugumi Ohba and Takeshi Obata (the writer and artist, respectively). These guys are now two of my favorite people.<br/><br/>In this book you will learn such things as L's real name *gasp* and other mind-blowing facts. Like the fact that Ohba didn't plan this series out at all before writing it.<br/><br/>WHAT. I know! How???<br/><br/>It </span>
  <span id="freeText1774045675034832344" style="display:none">Alright this is a really really good book to read once you've finished the Death Note series. It doesn't contain any more canon story, but it's full of character profiles and interviews with Tsugumi Ohba and Takeshi Obata (the writer and artist, respectively). These guys are now two of my favorite people.<br /><br />In this book you will learn such things as L's real name *gasp* and other mind-blowing facts. Like the fact that Ohba didn't plan this series out at all before writing it.<br /><br />WHAT. I know! How???<br /><br />It also contains the original pilot chapter that got this whole thing started. Also, a peek into the manga-making process, which is delicious for nerds like me.<br /><br />READ THIS PLEASE BECAUSE I NEED TO NERD OUT WITH <i>SOMEONE</i>. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tSFfM0HbtZzZVV963XVYarqHJgpeS0XpMNeYyTK5UHt64RVZEs2tCMzwZfEDPWACvM6cfXMQdsh//1rqpnv2iw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sZKx4hKOI4xTvF+kqbHU8dk6gkQBPiYMJSHDnOKc36l+UvuIQZg7GEYZZS93+eyZ33M4MyxlFS1qCQG/dl55WQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer1218888012397562643">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______' title='大場 つぐみ' rel='nofollow noopener'>大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br/><br/>There is spe</span>
  <span id="freeText1218888012397562643" style="display:none">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______" title="大場 つぐみ" rel="nofollow noopener">大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br /><br />There is speculation that Tsugumi Ōba is a pen name and that he is really Hiroshi Gamō. Pointing out that in Bakuman the main character's uncle was a one-hit wonder manga artist who worked on a gag super hero manga, very similar to Gamō and Tottemo! Luckyman in all aspects. Also that the storyboards drawn by Ōba greatly resemble Tottemo! Luckyman in style.</span>
